# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Storage Subsystem CSI Driver Integration

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the CSI driver integration: the CSI node plugin client, the CSI volume attach/detach controller, the CSI volume provisioner, and the PersistentVolume controller that bridges CSI operations to the core storage API.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

- `nodeinfomanager/nodeinfomanager.go` - CSI node info manager for CSINode lifecycle

- `attach_detach_controller.go` - Reconciles VolumeAttachment with CSI drivers

**3. PersistentVolume Controller (pkg/controller/volume/persistentvolume/)**
- `pv_controller.go` - Handles CSI dynamic provisioning and external provisioners
- `pv_controller_base.go` - Base controller with CSI migration support

],\n  \"text\": \"The Kubernetes CSI driver integration comprises a multi-layered architecture that bridges the core storage API with external Container Storage Interface drivers. The implementation is divided into several key components:\\n\\n## CSI Node Plugin Client (pkg/volume/csi/csi_client.go)\\nThe `csiClient` interface and its implementation `csiDriverClient` in pkg/volume/csi/csi_client.go provide the gRPC client for communicating with CSI drivers running on nodes. This is the foundation of the CSI plugin architecture. The interface defines critical node operations including:\\n- `NodePublishVolume()` - Makes a volume available at a mount path\\n- `NodeUnpublishVolume()` - Unmounts a volume\\n- `NodeStageVolume()` - Prepares a volume for use\\n- `NodeUnstageVolume()` - Cleans up volume staging\\n- `NodeExpandVolume()` - Handles volume expansion on the node\\n- `NodeGetInfo()` - Retrieves node topology and volume limits\\n\\nThe `newCsiDriverClient()` function creates connections to CSI drivers via gRPC, establishing long-lived connections that are monitored and reconnected as needed.\\n\\n## CSI Plugin Framework (pkg/volume/csi/csi_plugin.go)\\nThe main CSI plugin implementation in csi_plugin.go serves as the Kubernetes volume plugin that bridges volumes to CSI drivers. It implements the `volume.VolumePlugin` interface and provides the RegistrationHandler for dynamic plugin discovery. The `csiPlugin` struct maintains references to CSI drivers and orchestrates all CSI volume operations.\\n\\n## Volume Operations\\nThe CSI driver integration supports various volume operations through specialized implementations:\\n\\n1. **Mounting and Publishing (csi_mounter.go)**: The `csiMountMgr` handles volume mounting operations, implementing the `volume.Mounter` interface to stage and publish volumes to pod mount paths.\\n\\n2. **Attachment (csi_attacher.go)**: The `csiAttacher` struct implements both `volume.Attacher` and `volume.Detacher` interfaces, managing volume attachment operations through VolumeAttachment API objects. This integrates with the attach-detach controller.\\n\\n3. **Block Volumes (csi_block.go)**: The `csiBlockMapper` provides block volume support, implementing raw block device operations for CSI drivers that support block volumes.\\n\\n4. **Volume Expansion (expander.go)**: The `nodeExpandWithClient()` function implements volume expansion at the node level, coordinating with the CSI driver to resize mounted volumes.\\n\\n5. **Metrics (csi_metrics.go)**: The `metricsCsi` struct implements metrics collection for volumes, supporting NodeGetVolumeStats calls to CSI drivers.\\n\\n## CSI Node Information Management (pkg/volume/csi/nodeinfomanager/)\\nThe `nodeInfoManager` interface in nodeinfomanager.go manages the CSINode object lifecycle. It handles:\\n- Creating and updating CSINode objects with driver information\\n- Installing/uninstalling CSI drivers on nodes via CSINode.Spec.Drivers\\n- Managing topology information and volume allocatable limits\\n- Tracking CSI migration status for in-tree to CSI plugin migrations\\n\\nKey methods include `InstallCSIDriver()`, `UpdateCSIDriver()`, and `UninstallCSIDriver()`.\\n\\n## CSI Node Updater (pkg/volume/csi/csi_node_updater.go)\\nThe `csiNodeUpdater` watches CSIDriver objects and periodically updates CSINode with allocatable volume information based on the NodeAllocatableUpdatePeriodSeconds setting, ensuring accurate capacity tracking.\\n\\n## CSI Drivers Registry (pkg/volume/csi/csi_drivers_store.go)\\nThe `DriversStore` maintains a registry of all CSI drivers discovered on the node, tracking driver names, endpoints, and version information.\\n\\n## Volume Attach/Detach Controller (pkg/controller/volume/attachdetach/)\\nThe `attachDetachController` in attach_detach_controller.go integrates CSI attachment into the core Kubernetes attach-detach reconciliation loop. It:\\n- Maintains CSIDriver and CSINode informer listers\\n- Checks CSIDriver.Spec.AttachRequired to determine if VolumeAttachment is needed\\n- Integrates with the DesiredStateOfWorld and ActualStateOfWorld caches\\n- Coordinates attachment for both CSI and in-tree plugins\\n- Uses CSI migration support to translate in-tree volumes to CSI equivalents\\n\\nThe controller's primary entry point is `NewAttachDetachController()`, which sets up informer factories for CSINode and CSIDriver objects alongside traditional volume informers.\\n\\n## PersistentVolume Controller (pkg/controller/volume/persistentvolume/)\\nThe PersistentVolume controller in pv_controller.go and pv_controller_base.go bridges CSI provisioning with the Kubernetes core API:\\n- **Dynamic Provisioning**: Delegates to external provisioners for CSI drivers, allowing external-provisioner sidecars to handle volume creation\\n- **CSI Migration**: Uses `InTreeToCSITranslator` to translate in-tree volume specs to CSI equivalents\\n- **Volume Binding**: Coordinates with storage classes that reference CSI provisioners\\n- **Volume Status Tracking**: Manages provisioning state and error conditions\\n\\nKey methods in the provisioning flow include `provisionClaimOperationExternal()` which creates VolumeAttachment objects and coordinates with external-provisioner.\\n\\n## Architecture Summary\\nThe CSI driver integration creates a unified pathway:\\n1. StorageClass references CSI provisioner \u2192 External provisioner creates PV via CSI ControllerPublishVolume\\n2. Pod uses PVC \u2192 Attach-detach controller checks CSIDriver.AttachRequired\\n3. If attachment needed \u2192 VolumeAttachment CR triggers external-attacher via ControllerPublishVolume\\n4. On node \u2192 Kubelet uses CSI plugin to call NodeStageVolume \u2192 NodePublishVolume via gRPC\\n5. CSINode object tracks driver capabilities and volume limits\\n6. Migration layer automatically translates in-tree volumes to CSI when enabled\\n\\nThis design provides a clean separation between Kubernetes orchestration and storage driver implementation while maintaining backward compatibility through the migration framework.\"\n}\n",

The implementation is divided into several key components:\\n\\n## CSI Node Plugin Client (pkg/volume/csi/csi_client.go)\\nThe `csiClient` interface and its implementation `csiDriverClient` in pkg/volume/csi/csi_client.go provide the gRPC client for communicating with CSI drivers running on nodes. This is the foundation of the CSI plugin architecture. The interface defines critical node operations including:\\n- `NodePublishVolume()` - Makes a volume available at a mount path\\n- `NodeUnpublishVolume()` - Unmounts a volume\\n- `NodeStageVolume()` - Prepares a volume for use\\n- `NodeUnstageVolume()` - Cleans up volume staging\\n- `NodeExpandVolume()` - Handles volume expansion on the node\\n- `NodeGetInfo()` - Retrieves node topology and volume limits\\n\\nThe `newCsiDriverClient()` function creates connections to CSI drivers via gRPC, establishing long-lived connections that are monitored and reconnected as needed.\\n\\n## CSI Plugin Framework (pkg/volume/csi/csi_plugin.go)\\nThe main CSI plugin implementation in csi_plugin.go serves as the Kubernetes volume plugin that bridges volumes to CSI drivers. It implements the `volume.VolumePlugin` interface and provides the RegistrationHandler for dynamic plugin discovery. The `csiPlugin` struct maintains references to CSI drivers and orchestrates all CSI volume operations.\\n\\n## Volume Operations\\nThe CSI driver integration supports various volume operations through specialized implementations:\\n\\n1. **Mounting and Publishing (csi_mounter.go)**: The `csiMountMgr` handles volume mounting operations, implementing the `volume.Mounter` interface to stage and publish volumes to pod mount paths.\\n\\n2. **Attachment (csi_attacher.go)**: The `csiAttacher` struct implements both `volume.Attacher` and `volume.Detacher` interfaces, managing volume attachment operations through VolumeAttachment API objects. This integrates with the attach-detach controller.\\n\\n3. **Block Volumes (csi_block.go)**: The `csiBlockMapper` provides block volume support, implementing raw block device operations for CSI drivers that support block volumes.\\n\\n4. **Volume Expansion (expander.go)**: The `nodeExpandWithClient()` function implements volume expansion at the node level, coordinating with the CSI driver to resize mounted volumes.\\n\\n5. **Metrics (csi_metrics.go)**: The `metricsCsi` struct implements metrics collection for volumes, supporting NodeGetVolumeStats calls to CSI drivers.\\n\\n## CSI Node Information Management (pkg/volume/csi/nodeinfomanager/)\\nThe `nodeInfoManager` interface in nodeinfomanager.go manages the CSINode object lifecycle. It handles:\\n- Creating and updating CSINode objects with driver information\\n- Installing/uninstalling CSI drivers on nodes via CSINode.Spec.Drivers\\n- Managing topology information and volume allocatable limits\\n- Tracking CSI migration status for in-tree to CSI plugin migrations\\n\\nKey methods include `InstallCSIDriver()`, `UpdateCSIDriver()`, and `UninstallCSIDriver()`.\\n\\n## CSI Node Updater (pkg/volume/csi/csi_node_updater.go)\\nThe `csiNodeUpdater` watches CSIDriver objects and periodically updates CSINode with allocatable volume information based on the NodeAllocatableUpdatePeriodSeconds setting, ensuring accurate capacity tracking.\\n\\n## CSI Drivers Registry (pkg/volume/csi/csi_drivers_store.go)\\nThe `DriversStore` maintains a registry of all CSI drivers discovered on the node, tracking driver names, endpoints, and version information.\\n\\n## Volume Attach/Detach Controller (pkg/controller/volume/attachdetach/)\\nThe `attachDetachController` in attach_detach_controller.go integrates CSI attachment into the core Kubernetes attach-detach reconciliation loop. It:\\n- Maintains CSIDriver and CSINode informer listers\\n- Checks CSIDriver.Spec.AttachRequired to determine if VolumeAttachment is needed\\n- Integrates with the DesiredStateOfWorld and ActualStateOfWorld caches\\n- Coordinates attachment for both CSI and in-tree plugins\\n- Uses CSI migration support to translate in-tree volumes to CSI equivalents\\n\\nThe controller's primary entry point is `NewAttachDetachController()`, which sets up informer factories for CSINode and CSIDriver objects alongside traditional volume informers.\\n\\n## PersistentVolume Controller (pkg/controller/volume/persistentvolume/)\\nThe PersistentVolume controller in pv_controller.go and pv_controller_base.go bridges CSI provisioning with the Kubernetes core API:\\n- **Dynamic Provisioning**: Delegates to external provisioners for CSI drivers, allowing external-provisioner sidecars to handle volume creation\\n- **CSI Migration**: Uses `InTreeToCSITranslator` to translate in-tree volume specs to CSI equivalents\\n- **Volume Binding**: Coordinates with storage classes that reference CSI provisioners\\n- **Volume Status Tracking**: Manages provisioning state and error conditions\\n\\nKey methods in the provisioning flow include `provisionClaimOperationExternal()` which creates VolumeAttachment objects and coordinates with external-provisioner.\\n\\n## Architecture Summary\\nThe CSI driver integration creates a unified pathway:\\n1. StorageClass references CSI provisioner \u2192 External provisioner creates PV via CSI ControllerPublishVolume\\n2. Pod uses PVC \u2192 Attach-detach controller checks CSIDriver.AttachRequired\\n3. If attachment needed \u2192 VolumeAttachment CR triggers external-attacher via ControllerPublishVolume\\n4. On node \u2192 Kubelet uses CSI plugin to call NodeStageVolume \u2192 NodePublishVolume via gRPC\\n5. CSINode object tracks driver capabilities and volume limits\\n6. Migration layer automatically translates in-tree volumes to CSI when enabled\\n\\nThis design provides a clean separation between Kubernetes orchestration and storage driver implementation while maintaining backward compatibility through the migration framework.\"\n}\n",
